(3) Awards Ceremony

After the scores were calculated at 4:30 PM, the awards ceremony was held immediately. The Party song was sung, and the ceremony was performed. After respectfully reading the will, Chairman Xu (Director of the Education Bureau) delivered the closing speech. Secretary-General Yu of the Municipal Government, representing the Mayor, delivered a speech, and then Mrs. Yu presented the awards separately. The winning children were filled with joy, and the onlookers applauded and cheered. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

▲ Director Xu's Closing Speech

Director Xu said, "Today is the closing day of the third joint sports meet of municipal elementary schools. I hope that the sports performance of each elementary school will be better year after year, and the physical condition will be better year after year, as I said at the opening ceremony. Now, the results have been compiled, and most of the records are higher than last year. This is not only an honor for the schools, but also closely related to the municipal government, this bureau, and the entire society of Shanghai. If various results are declining instead of improving, what is the effect of the year's physical training of the city's elementary schools? How regrettable! Therefore, my first hope is that the physical education of municipal elementary schools will progress every year, breaking the records of the second time in the third time, and breaking the records of the third time in the fourth time, forever progressing. My second hope is that all of you children will get the foundation of physical training in your childhood, and continue to do so. As you grow older, your sports performance will also improve. The physical education of Japan is because they pay attention to it step by step from childhood, so they can dominate the Far East and occupy a considerable position in the world sports games. The result of our country's representatives in the Far Eastern Games is like this. If we participate in the World Sports Games, we can imagine what will happen. This is truly a great shame. Shanghai is a culturally developed area, and it should show something in sports. I hope that the current elementary school students will train hard and compete in the Far Eastern Games and the World Sports Games in a few years to come, and bring glory to the Republic of China. Finally, I would like to thank all sectors of society for their numerous awards, and I am deeply grateful for their sincerity in promoting sports. I would also like to sincerely thank the judges, the Boy Scout band, and the ambulance team for their hard work for three consecutive days to achieve this successful result."

▲ Mayor's Representative's Speech

Secretary-General Yu said, "Today is the closing of the Municipal Elementary School Joint Sports Meet, and I am deeply honored to participate in the awards ceremony on behalf of the Mayor. In recent days, my colleagues in the Municipal Government have paid close attention to the Municipal Elementary School Joint Sports Meet. Seeing the excellent results reported in the newspapers, we are deeply pleased. This is a testament to the efforts of the principals and teachers in their daily training. Today's awards to the children are proof of their attention to exercise and their excellent results. I hope that those who win the awards will continue to practice and strive for perfection, and that those who do not win the awards will also be guided by the principles of peace and struggle, work harder, and strive for victory in the future."

Local News

British Aviatrix Miss [Sheila] Scott Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday

▲Flew from Xiamen to Shanghai in Eight Hours ▲Will Continue to Japan Tomorrow

The first female long-distance pilot to arrive in Shanghai, British aviator Miss [Sheila] Scott, flew her single-engine plane, undertaking the long-distance flight from London to Tokyo, and arrived safely at Hongqiao Airport yesterday at 2 PM. If the weather is favorable, she plans to fly to Hiroshima, Japan, tomorrow morning, before continuing to Tokyo. Miss [Sheila] Scott is currently staying at the residence of the British Consul-General, [John] Brenan.

▲Grand Welcome. Miss [Sheila] Scott flew from Hong Kong to Xiamen this past Wednesday. Yesterday morning at 6 AM, she flew from Xiamen to Shanghai. The foreign community in Shanghai prepared a welcome, expecting Miss [Sheila] Scott to arrive at noon. The British Consul-General's representative, [G.] Brander, the Shanghai Women's Association, and representatives of the Royal Aero Club of Great Britain, numbering about a hundred people, gathered at Hongqiao Airport, waiting until 1 PM, but Miss [Sheila] Scott's plane had not yet appeared. There were reports that Miss [Sheila] Scott had landed in Hangzhou. The British Consul-General's representative, [G.] Brander, discussed with the airplane factory director, Shen Dexie, who then personally flew a red military aircraft to scout the sky and welcome her from the direction of Hangzhou.

▲Sudden Arrival. Just as the welcoming ladies were eagerly anticipating her arrival, Miss [Sheila] Scott's small silver-gray plane suddenly appeared in the sky at 1:58 PM. The welcoming ladies, upon seeing it, rushed into the airport. Miss [Sheila] Scott flew around once in the air, then landed safely at 2 PM amidst applause and cheers. The crowd immediately surrounded her and dozens of cameras competed to take photographs. Miss [Sheila] Scott, of petite stature, wearing a flight suit, shook hands and spoke with the welcomers, her face beaming with smiles.

Miss [Sheila] Scott Arrives in Shanghai for Photography

Although she looked slightly weary from the eight-hour flight in the air yesterday, her spirits were still quite lively. The entire plane was covered with well wishes from people from the places she had traveled through. After a while, the plane that had gone to greet her returned. British Consul [G.] Brander then introduced Miss [Sheila] Scott to factory director Shen and expressed his gratitude for the welcome. Consul [G.] Brander then escorted Miss [Sheila] Scott to the British Consulate. After Miss [Sheila] Scott landed, Public Security Bureau representative Qu Xunyi and airplane factory representative Zhu Jiaren, in addition to expressing their welcome, originally intended to inspect Miss [Sheila] Scott's plane according to regulations, but considering Miss [Sheila] Scott's fatigue, they postponed it.

▲Flying East Tomorrow. Miss [Sheila] Scott departed from London alone on September 25, originally planning to fly to Tokyo in fifteen days. However, after flying through Europe, she encountered difficulties and had to make an emergency landing in the Persian Gulf, where she was held captive by Arabs. Miss [Sheila] Scott entertained the Arabs with song and dance to avoid danger. After flying to Hong Kong, she fell from a horse with the Governor of Hong Kong and was injured. Flying from Hong Kong to Xiamen, she had another close call when a leak developed in her plane's fuel tank. Fortunately, she landed safely in Xiamen. The wing was slightly damaged and, after minor repairs, she flew to Shanghai yesterday morning at 6 AM. The nearly two thousand-mile flight from Xiamen to Shanghai was one of the most difficult legs of her entire journey. After eight hours of flight, she finally arrived safely in Shanghai. After arriving in Shanghai, Miss [Sheila] Scott told this newspaper's reporter that the weather was clear when she departed from Xiamen, but she soon encountered headwinds and dense fog, making it impossible to discern her direction. She was forced to fly along the coast, causing her to arrive in Shanghai later than expected. She now plans to leave Shanghai on Sunday morning and fly east, first to Hiroshima, then to Tokyo. If the route proves too difficult, she will first fly to Korea before proceeding to Tokyo.

Internal and External Debt Consolidation Conference Opens in Beijing Today

▲Dutch and Italian Consuls Arrive in Beijing Last Night

Rumors that the Internal and External Debt Consolidation Committee would meet in Shanghai on the 14th are completely inaccurate. Various Customs Inspection Vessels

▲Recapture of the Right to Appoint Ship Inspectors ▲Increase in Inspection Vessel Fees

The Shanghai shipping industry's request to recapture the right to appoint ship inspectors for the Jianghai Customs has been underway. Now, the Customs has announced an increase in inspection vessel fees. The various rumors heard are recorded as follows:

▲Expiration of the Englishman's Contract. The ship inspector for the Jianghai Customs is an Englishman named McNy, whose contract is for thirty-five years. There are also four English assistants. All Chinese and foreign merchant ships must be inspected by them once a year. The seaworthiness of the ship is stated in the inspector's certificate. After a ship has been inspected, the shipowner's responsibility in terms of navigation is greatly reduced. In the event of an accident, it can be attributed to circumstances beyond human control, so that the insurance company does not resist payment. Now, the Englishman's thirty-five-year contract will expire next spring. The Shanghai shipping industry is therefore striving to have a Chinese person appointed as his successor.

▲Ministry of Communications Has Agreed to Issue Certificates. There are quite a few Chinese who have experience in ship inspection and are capable of holding this position. At present, the Shanghai shipping industry has nominated six people, but there are still some discrepancies in the procedures regarding the certificates. The Shanghai shipping industry has submitted a request to the Ministry of Communications to draft and issue regulations for the issuance and registration of ship inspector certificates so that Chinese people can apply for them and serve in this capacity in various customs offices. The Ministry of Communications has approved the request of the Shanghai shipping industry to draft these regulations, which will be submitted to the National Government for promulgation after the draft is completed. This should be implemented soon. ▲Customs Increases Inspection Vessel Fees. The Shanghai Jianghai Customs has announced an increase in inspection vessel fees and has notified the shipping companies to comply. The new and old rates are listed below (the table uses Customs registered tonnage as the unit of measure, the new price is the original rate plus the increase, and the unit is taels):

Tonnage / New Price / Original Rate / Increase

Within 50 tons / 30 / 20 / 10

50 to 75 tons / 40 / 30 / 10

76 to 100 tons / 60 / 40 / 20

101 to 150 tons / 75 / 50 / 25

151 to 250 tons / 100 / 75 / 25

251 to 500 tons / 125 / 100 / 25

501 to 1000 tons / 150 / 125 / 25

1001 to 200 tons / 200 / 125 / 75

201 to 2000 tons / 250 / 125 / 125

Over 2000 tons / 300 / 125 / 175

The Prerequisite for Regulating People's Food Supply

▲Planning and Building Perfect Rice Warehouses

The 20th regular meeting of the Municipal Food Committee was held today at the Social Affairs Bureau. Feng Liutang, chairman of the committee, proposed that the construction of rice warehouses should be the first step in regulating the people's food supply and restoring warehousing. The original text reads: "The system of famine relief is found in the Zhou Dynasty's 'Ever-Normal Granary' theory, which originated in the Warring States period. From the Han Dynasty through the Sui Dynasty to the Song Dynasty, the three-warehouse system was fully established, but it was constantly rising and falling. By the Qing Dynasty, money was accumulated instead of grain, so when famine suddenly occurred, there was no preparation. The original intention of accumulating money must have been to learn from the drawbacks of accumulating grain or to consider other uses (such as the Green Sprouts Policy). In fact, the system of accumulating grain is not bad, but it is due to the badness of people and the badness of politics. If people are bad and politics are bad, even if there is a good system, it cannot be implemented. For example, the social granaries were good when Zhu Xi implemented them, but later generations saw their drawbacks. This is what should be emphasized in both governing people and governing laws. Now, after years of frequent famine, everyone knows the necessity of restoring warehousing. The municipal warehousing fund is already being planned and raised. How the fundraising will succeed cannot be predicted, but it will definitely be able to raise some money. Its use should be waited for after the funds are in place, but what can be said is that accumulating grain is better than accumulating money, because accumulating grain can achieve an ever-normal granary, can achieve price stabilization, and can also provide disaster relief. The local situation can be considered (such as the difference between Shanghai and the interior, and even within Shanghai, the necessity of handling the urban area and the rural area separately), as well as the degree of famine. If money is accumulated, it must be raised at the time of the event, which easily misses the opportunity, and the handling is cumbersome, and the losses are more extensive. This can be verified by recent events. Whether it is accumulating grain or accumulating money, warehouses are needed. In the past, the construction of rice warehouses in our country can be seen in Zhang Zhaorui's 'Fixed Granary Foundation Style'. The planning was never not thorough, but it still could not be completed. Birds eat and insects bore because the architecture is not modern and complete. For example, Shanghai rice merchants have not stockpiled as much rice in recent years as in the past, which is certainly due to the high cost of warehouse rent and land prices. However, the construction of warehouses was originally intended for the storage of general commercial goods, and it is not suitable to store rice in them. Moreover, there are no suitable warehouses that can be used for storing rice. In the event of continuous rainy days, the rice will not be sufficient, and the rice price will immediately rise. The citizens of Shanghai have lived in this unstable life for a long time. If there were perfect rice warehouses, how could it be to this extent? Recently, it has been seen that the old coarse rice imported from Japan is oily and shiny, just like new rice. If our country's rice is stored for one year, it will be covered with insects and ash. After two or three years, it will turn into dust. Therefore, without the construction of perfect rice warehouses, there is no grain to store, and storage will cause a lot of loss. It can be seen from this that regulating grain and maintaining the people's food supply depends on having storage, and storage requires the construction of perfect rice warehouses. Now, when this city is preparing to restore warehousing, I propose that rice warehouses be built first when the fundraising for the fund is successful, and the following methods are attached: (1) Collect drawings of perfect rice warehouses, or send personnel to foreign countries to conduct on-site investigations of the architectural style of rice warehouses and their management methods. (2) Allocate several tens of thousands of yuan from the warehousing fund to serve as a construction fund (the amount must be determined by construction engineers). (3) Request the Municipal Government to allocate public land on the Pujiang coast, and the location should be selected where large ships can berth. If there is no public land, then encircle and purchase private land. (4) When building rice warehouses, the wharves and their lifting and unloading equipment must be built together. (5) Rice warehouses should be divided into several parts, so that when the public sector has surplus storage, it can be transferred to merchants for storage. Is the above method feasible? I hope for a public decision."

After signing the Sino-Czech commercial treaty, the Czech Chargé d'Affaires, Ni Cidu, requested leave to return to his country and ask for government approval. Yesterday afternoon at 4:30, he visited the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Office and met with Chen Shiguang and Liu Yunfang to announce his assumption of office. He also said that the Sino-Czech commercial treaty had been approved by the government, appointing him as the plenipotentiary representative. He will go to Beijing in the coming days to visit Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting and officially sign the Sino-Czech commercial treaty on behalf of the Czech government. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs Office has already reported this to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.

Former US Minister Crane Departs Shanghai Yesterday

Former US Minister to China, Mr. Crane, came to Shanghai the day before yesterday and stayed at the Cathay Hotel on the Bund. He left China yesterday afternoon at 3 PM aboard the Empress of Russia. Those who saw him off included Minister Kong's wife, Xu Jianping, Zhu Shaoping, Zhao Guocai, and his wife, among others. It is reported that Mr. Crane hosted a banquet for He Bingsong and others at the Cathay Hotel the night before last. Mr. Crane, who is seventy-two years old, was in good spirits and talked at length until 11 PM. Someone asked him what his feelings were about this trip, and he said that after the war ended, everything could be revived, and although China was in the midst of war, its progress was also very rapid.

Japanese Business Group Comes to China for Investigation

The Continental Daily reports that a group of representatives from various business organizations in Osaka, accompanied by two officials from the Osaka Prefectural Government's Commerce Section, will arrive in Shanghai at the end of this month. It is reported that the purpose of this trip is to investigate the commercial situation in Shanghai and the Yangtze River area. The main issues to be investigated are: (1) The decline in silver prices and the situation in Shanghai; (2) The impact of the civil war on the supply and demand of goods; (3) The competition between Japanese and foreign goods; (4) The situation of Chinese industry and inland finance. Last year, Osaka's sales to China, including the Yangtze River basin and Shanghai, totaled 10,584,000 Japanese yen. The 200 items transported from Shanghai to Osaka amounted to 2,578,000 Japanese yen.

(2) The business that the city should handle must be carried out in a practical manner. The implementation of important projects and the adjustment of finances should be planned. It is hoped that the various bureaus will pay close attention and study them carefully. As soon as the speaker returns to Shanghai, they can be discussed and implemented in order. (3) During Director Chen of the Education Bureau's absence from duty, all bureau affairs have been delegated to Councilor Xu. It is hoped that Acting Director Xu will have a thorough reform plan to comfort expectations. 2. Secretary-General's report: (1) Regarding the provisions of Article 5 of the Labor Dispute Resolution Law, the parties may file a lawsuit with the court in accordance with the law if they wish to object after accepting the decision of the arbitration committee. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce has approved the notification of the Executive Yuan, which has been forwarded to the government and has been forwarded to the relevant parties. It has been handed over to the five bureaus of Social Affairs, Finance, Public Security, Port Affairs, and Public Utilities for verification and deliberation, and it should be banned. A letter has been sent and an order for the ban has been issued. (3) The amendment to the Municipal Road Construction Fee Regulations was previously approved by the Municipal Meeting. Now, the Secretariat has raised reasons and requested a review, which has been approved. It has been included in the agenda of this session. Please pay attention. 3. The bureau chiefs and councilors have separate mimeographed reports. B. Discussion Items: (1) The case of the expiration of the contract for the construction of the Shanghai West Water Supply by the China Merchants, and no one bidding, it was resolved that the third step should be taken and the Public Utilities Bureau should be responsible for handling it. (2) Review and amendment of the Municipal Road Construction Fee Regulations was resolved to pass the second amendment.

Joint Meeting of All Trade Unions in the City

▲Support the Permanent Organization of Trade Unions ▲Resolved to Jointly Send a Telegram Requesting the Fourth Plenary Session

▲Declaration Issued by the Delegation Petitioning in Beijing

Yesterday afternoon at 2 PM, all two hundred trade unions in the city held a joint meeting in support of the permanent organization of trade unions. Those present included representatives from the British American Tobacco Factory Trade Union, Huacheng Tobacco Factory Trade Union, Shanghai Mercerizing Industry Trade Union, Postal Workers Union, Huashang Electric Trade Union, Commercial Press Trade Union, Press Trade Union, Silk and Satin Dyeing Trade Union, Western Furniture Trade Union, Lianglu Catering Trade Union, and various other trade unions in the city, totaling more than one hundred organizations and more than two hundred representatives. Yang Youren, chairman of the Commercial Press Trade Union, was elected to chair the meeting. After the formalities, the chairman first reported that since the Ministry of Industry and Commerce promulgated Article 10 of the Implementation Law of Trade Associations, which restricts trade union members to elect one representative to join the trade association for every fifteen or more people, all the trade unions in the city were panicked. A joint meeting was convened and representatives were sent to Beijing to petition the Fourth Plenary Session. The results are still unknown. However, the various trade unions in the city have not yet made a substantial statement of mutual concern as workers, so today a joint meeting of all trade unions in the city is held to support the existence of trade unions. I hope that all representatives present will express their opinions as much as possible to seek ways to help. The agenda was then discussed: (1) Each trade union will jointly submit a petition to the Fourth Plenary Session requesting the promulgation of separate laws and regulations for trade unions. (2) All economic problems will be temporarily covered by each trade union. (3) The Postal Workers Union and the Commercial Press Trade Union will be responsible for drafting the written communication. (4) The signing of the petition will be divided into six major areas, with each area responsible for signing by two trade unions: South Shanghai, Zhabei, Pudong, West Shanghai, East Shanghai, and Central Shanghai. (5) The written communication will be sent by telegram tomorrow (the 15th) and the petition will be sent on the 17th. (6) The telegram from the trade union representatives petitioning in Beijing will be published in various newspapers. The meeting adjourned at 6 PM. The declaration is copied below: "Since the various trade unions in Shanghai heard that the central government had a message to abolish the staff unions and merge them into the trade associations, the various trade unions publicly elected representatives to go to Beijing on the 25th of last month to petition the central government and various organs. Although the central government took into consideration the hidden feelings of the staff members and allowed the abolition to be temporarily delayed, which showed consideration for public opinion and accommodation of public opinion, the word 'temporary' still belongs to a swallow's nest on the curtain, which is not safe for long. Therefore, hundreds of thousands of staff members in the city are panicked and worried. Therefore, after internal and external troubles, the various trade unions in the city have no choice but to elect Hu Shouqi of the Calligraphy and Painting Fan Trade Union, Zhao Zhenhui of the Pharmaceutical Trade Union, Zhu Xiaoyun of the Silk and Cloth Dyeing Trade Union, Yu Yaoqiu of the Taikang Food Trade Union, Weng Ruifu of the Sauce Trade Union, Cai Xiaohe of the Tea Trade Union, and Sang Yutang of the Pharmaceutical Trade Union as representatives to go to Beijing with a petition to make a final petition to the Fourth Plenary Session. I secretly thought that the Fourth Plenary Session is a meeting to reform politics and strive for construction. For events that should be promoted and reformed in the country, it can especially be based on the intention of a single word to revitalize the country. Whether the organization of our staff unions is determined is not only related to the hopes of the people, but also to the country. It is impossible to make a part of the people feel frustrated. I think the advanced parties and countries in the Fourth Plenary Session will be able to consider the situation and consider the feelings of the people. The organization of trade unions should be promulgated as soon as possible, and the separate laws and regulations for staff members should be determined as soon as possible. The people who were oppressed by warlords in the past were revived by the Fourth Plenary Session of the revolutionary government, which was watered by a sprig of Yang Zhi. How can their songs of praise and virtue only let Yao Tian Shunri be beautiful in the past? I dare to reveal my feelings in the hope that the authorities will adopt them. This is a declaration, and I beg you to judge it."

The Directorate General of Posts Cables to Negotiate the Return of Russian-Detained Mail

During the conflict between China and Russia, the mail sent from this port to various places, all those passing through the Soviet Russian region, were detained by the Russian side, totaling more than one hundred bags. Since the end of the Sino-Russian conflict, although the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has repeatedly negotiated with the Soviet Russian authorities for its return, there has been no reply from the other side so far. The Directorate General of Posts believes that most of the detained mail is registered and express mail. If it is lost due to detention, it will inevitably be blamed by most senders. Therefore, it yesterday sent a telegram to the Ministry of Communications, asking it to quickly consult the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and actively negotiate to ensure that all the detained mail of more than one hundred bags is returned.

Silk Factory Opening Dispute

The Shanghai silk industry is suffering losses, leading to factory closures. The livelihoods of over ten thousand workers are at stake. As a result of negotiations, thirty-two factories are reopening with reduced burdens. This has been reported in our newspaper. On the 11th, thirty silk factories in various districts convened representatives of male and female workers, informing them of the factories' difficulties and the efforts being made to resume operations to support the workers' livelihoods. The factories stated that they would lose at least two hundred taels of silver for each bale of silk purchased and would incur more losses for each day of operation. At the time, the female workers' representatives expressed agreement, only requesting that wages be increased once the price of silk in foreign markets improved and exceeded one thousand taels. The factories agreed to this. Workers in other districts also understood and accepted the situation. However, a small number of workers in the Hongkou district raised objections, demanding that all factories reopen simultaneously instead of just a few initially. On the evening of the 12th, they secretly forced mechanics and firemen in the nine silk factories scheduled to reopen in the Hongkou district to sign documents prohibiting them from lighting the furnaces or providing power. Later, Zhu Jing'an, a standing committee member of the industry association, offered earnest advice, and the workers eventually complied. Unexpectedly, yesterday morning (the 14th), more than ten factories in the Zhabei, Xin Zha, and Hudong districts that were preparing to reopen resumed work as usual. However, in the Hongkou district, as the nine factories scheduled to reopen were lighting their furnaces and starting their machines, a man named Chen Zhongxiang (an employee of the Yichang Silk Factory) led a group of people to each factory to prevent them from starting their furnaces. Later, at the Yuanfeng Silk Factory on Dixiwei Road, they forced all factory employees to sign documents prohibiting the resumption of work and threatened the factory manager, Wang Zaisheng, saying that if the factory reopened, there would be bloodshed. The factory owner arrived and tried to persuade Chen and his group, but Chen was disrespectful and made many threatening remarks. The police detectives stationed at the factory witnessed the situation and considered Chen Zhongxiang's actions to be unlawful, as he was openly preventing the factories from reopening and obstructing the workers' livelihoods. Furthermore, they discovered that Chen Zhongxiang was a subversive element who was already wanted by the garrison headquarters. Now, he was inciting the public to coerce a strike and intimidating the factory owners, which could not be tolerated. They planned to arrest him, but Chen attempted to escape to avoid punishment. The police pursued and apprehended him, taking him to the third precinct of the fifth district. After a short time, he was transferred to the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau for further investigation. In the afternoon, dozens of employees who sympathized with Chen Zhongxiang gathered at the third precinct of the fifth district, surrounding it on all sides and demanding Chen Zhongxiang's release. The precinct chief, Zhang, explained that Chen had already been handed over to the police bureau. The employees then went to the Silk Industry Association, demanding that Chen Zhongxiang be released before any negotiations on reopening the factories could take place. The standing committee members of the association refused, stating that the authority to release Chen lay with the government and that they had no power to intervene. The employees, unable to achieve their objective, left in frustration. After receiving reports of the disturbances from various factories, the Industry Association, in addition to submitting reports to higher authorities requesting protection, also sent Chairman Shen and others to the municipal party headquarters, the municipal government, the social bureau, and the public security bureau to personally explain the situation.

Startling Imports of Japanese Artificial Silk

▲One of the Reasons for the Silk Industry's Decline ▲Potentially Exceeding 30 Million Yuan This Year

According to a recent investigation, the Chinese silk industry has declined sharply in recent years, while imports of artificial silk from various countries have increased dramatically. This indicates the wide distribution of artificial silk in the country. Considering Japan alone, from January to September of this year, the total export of artificial silk nationwide exceeded 23 million yuan. It is estimated that by the end of the year, this figure could increase to over 35 million yuan. Among these, 1,805 bales were imported to Shanghai, with a value of 988,000 yuan, and 3,781 bales were imported through Hong Kong, with a value of 1.443 million yuan.

Guarantee Required for Obtaining Passports for Overseas Travel

▲To Avoid Being Repatriated

The municipal government approved a letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, stating that in recent years, there have been cases of Chinese citizens being repatriated after obtaining passports for overseas travel. The Ministry, aware of this issue, has stipulated in Article 9 of the Provisional Regulations for Passports that a firm guarantee is required before a passport can be issued to prevent such incidents from happening again. Therefore, going forward, the regulations will be strictly enforced to rectify this problem. The municipal government instructed the Public Security Bureau to comply with these instructions yesterday.

Local News II

British Merchant Ship Turns Around, Causing Major Disaster

▲Two Pier Sections Collapse into the River ▲More Than Ten Civilian Boats Capsized

▲Cook's Apprentice Wu Fulin Dies Tragically ▲Losses on All Sides are Substantial

The merchant ship *City of Johannesburg*, belonging to the British trading firm Jardine Matheson, was loading cargo in Shanghai yesterday for export to England and Germany. While turning around in the Huangpu River, it struck and damaged the Mitsubishi wharf where Nisshin Kisen's ships are docked, and also caused multiple cargo boats to sink, drowning one boatman. The details of this incident are reported as follows:

▲British Ship Strikes Pier

At 8:35 AM yesterday, the British ship *City of Johannesburg* departed from the Jardine Matheson wharf, being towed by a Wheelock & Co. tugboat. To turn the ship around, it was towed in front of the Sanyang Wharf of the Nisshin Kisen Company (also known as the Mitsubishi Wharf, where ships to Luoyang, Yueyang, and Nanyang are docked). Although the river is wide at that point, the current is the strongest, and accidents are not uncommon. As the *City of Johannesburg* was turning in front of the wharf, the tugboat had already turned its head, but the bow of the large ship, affected by the tide, lost its direction and crashed into the southern pier of the Nisshin Kisen Wharf. Due to the massive impact, the pier suddenly shifted north, and two pier sections collapsed into the river due to the loss of support. This area is lined with cargo ships loading goods for the Japan Mail Line and fishing boats. The collapse of the pier and the impact of the ship caused a major disaster.

▲Cargo Barges and Fishing Boats Capsize

The area where the pier sections collapsed was on the inner side of the wharf, where six salvage boats were docked. These six boats were destroyed by the pressure of the collapse. On the eastern side, civilian boats carrying export cargo for the Japan Mail Line ship *Asama Maru* were docked. As the pier collapsed into the water and the southern pier was pushed north by the British ship by several zhang, four cargo boats belonging to Wu Minggen, Shen Rongfa, and others, which were carrying rapeseed and cotton yarn, were crushed or sunk outside the *Asama Maru*. The cargo of sesame and cotton yarn was lost in the water, causing huge losses. The hulls of the boats were also severely damaged. Wu Fulin, a boatman from Wu Minggen's boat, fell into the water and drowned before he could be rescued.

▲Losses Estimated to Be Significant

A total of ten cargo barges and fishing boats inside and outside the pier were struck, damaged, or capsized by the British ship. Fortunately, there were many boats nearby that came to the rescue, and the boatmen who fell into the water were rescued first. The cargo that fell into the water was also salvaged urgently. Fifty bales of cotton yarn, loaded by the Japan Cotton Yarn Co., were all recovered, and about two hundred bags of sesame were also partially recovered. In total, the damaged boats on the inner side of the pier included six fishing boats belonging to Zhao Jiayu and others, as well as one Jiangbei boat belonging to Liu Bucheng. In the middle of the two piers, three wharf boats belonging to Shen Xinhua, Wu Minggen, and Qian Afu were damaged. According to the loss reports submitted by the various boat owners, (1) Wu Minggen's boat suffered losses of 2,500 yuan, (2) Shen Rongfa's and Shen Shenshi's boats suffered combined losses of over 1,900 yuan, (3) Shen Zhongfu suffered losses of 850 yuan, (5) Liu Bucheng suffered losses of 259 yuan, (6) Shen Rufa suffered losses of 73 yuan. The loss amounts from Shen Hualin and others have not yet been reported.

▲Drowned Boatman Sent for Autopsy

Wu Fulin, son of Wu Minggen, was only seventeen years old. He worked on the boat and fell into the river when the boat was struck and overturned. After being retrieved by the water patrol captain and the police with the help of his father, he had already drowned due to ingesting too much water. The water patrol captain sent the body to the Rescue Bureau for an autopsy and then returned it to the family for burial.

▲Water Police Assist in Rescue

After the incident, the First Squad of the Water Patrol received the news and immediately dispatched patrolmen Song Kuiyuan, Ren Jianming, and others to assist in the rescue. Afterwards, a reporter met with Liu Qimin, an officer of the Water Patrol Headquarters, who provided an account of the incident and a report on the actions taken by the team.

At 9:45 AM on the 14th of this month, a sailor named Jin Qianlong reported that a British merchant ship belonging to Jardine Matheson had damaged the Mitsubishi Wharf while turning around for export, and also damaged multiple cargo boats and fishing boats carrying foreign yarn. Police officers Sun Deqi and others were already assisting in the rescue and salvage efforts. Patrol officers Song Kuiyuan, Ren Jianming, Hou Buyun, Cheng Xuyuan, Lu Songxin, and others were immediately dispatched to assist in the rescue and salvage efforts. Hired laborers were used to salvage the cargo. A total of 50 bales of foreign yarn and 100+ bags of sesame were recovered. The sesame boat owner, Wu Minggen, was brought in for questioning. He stated that his boat had loaded 220 bags of sesame at Laogang yesterday and was docked between the north and south piers of the Mitsubishi Wharf this morning, intending to unload it onto the Japanese ship *Asama Maru*. However, at 8:35 AM, a British ship belonging to Jardine Matheson suddenly struck the southern pier while turning around for export. The pier was pushed northward by several zhang, damaging the civilian boat and causing approximately 200 bags of sesame to fall into the water. At the same time, Wu Minggen's 17-year-old son, Wu Fulin, was knocked into the water and drowned. After being retrieved, he was already dead. The officer personally went to the wharf to conduct a detailed inspection. It was found that the north and south wooden piers were approximately four zhang apart. Wu Minggen and others' boats were docked south of the northern pier. After being struck, the southern pier was pushed northward by more than three zhang and westward by about one zhang. The damage included six fishing boats belonging to Zhao Jiabao and others inside the pier, one Jiangbei boat belonging to Liu Bucheng, and three wharf boats belonging to Shen Xinhua, Wu Minggen, and Qian Afu between the two piers. Instructions were given to the respective boat owners to submit a list of losses, and a separate report was to be submitted. The body of Wu Fulin was to be sent to the Rescue Bureau for an autopsy. A report was duly submitted.

▲British Ship Immediately Leaves Port

After the incident, the British ship immediately left the port, as only a small portion of its bow was damaged. The affected boatmen are negotiating compensation with Jardine Matheson through official channels, as well as requesting funeral expenses for the deceased. The Nisshin Kisen Wharf, which was severely damaged by the ship, is assessing the damage and will also negotiate compensation with Jardine Matheson while making repairs.

Water Police Suppress Pirates

▲Hundreds of Pirate Ships ▲Residents Flee Empty-Handed ▲Infighting Among Pirate Leaders

On the 8th, in the waters outside Wusongkou, such as Fengli, Juegang, and Changsha, a large number of pirate ships, estimated at over one hundred, suddenly appeared from the north and south. The total number of pirates was estimated to be over two thousand. After the pirate ships concentrated in those waters, bugle calls and gunfire were frequently heard for several days. Although no one has landed to cause trouble, they have not yet left. Residents living along the coast in those areas are terrified. Families with even a small amount of wealth are afraid that the pirates will land and loot their homes, so they are fleeing to other places en masse, leaving many homes empty. The water and land police stationed in those areas are too weak to suppress them, so they have sent urgent telegrams to the Fourth District Seventeenth Squad of the Wusong Water Police and various counties such as Rugao and Haimen, warning them of the situation. They have also dug ditches of several zhang along the village roads, pedestrian paths, and crossroads at various ports to obstruct traffic, concentrating their forces at key points to maintain strict vigilance day and night to prevent any eventuality. However, according to news from the Water Police yesterday, the pirates have not yet landed to loot. It is said that a dispute over the distribution of spoils occurred between the two major pirate leaders, Shen Guanxi and Pan Kaiwu. As a result, another group of pirates has invited both parties to meet in those waters to mediate. If the negotiations fail, a fierce battle will ensue. Captain Gong of the Seventeenth Squad of the Water Police has dispatched a patrol ship to take advantage of the situation and suppress the pirates.

News of the Support Xiao Rally

▲Enthusiastic Participation in Joining the Organizers ▲Overseas Chinese Federation Decides to Wait Several More Days

The Overseas Chinese Federation sent a letter to various organizations requesting them to initiate and convene an all-sector rally to discuss methods for "Supporting Xiao, Eradicating Shame, and Resolving the Suffering of Overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies." The news has been reported in this newspaper. It has been learned that the federation has received replies from organizations such as the Chinese Overseas Chinese Affairs Advancement Association, the China Vocational Education Society, the Shanghai Vocational Guidance Center, the Chinese Seamen's Industrial Joint General Association, the Taiwan Chinese General Association, the Shanghai Law School, the Yixing Fellow-Townsmen Association, the Xiao Case Support Association of Yixing Sojourners in Shanghai, and the Shanghai National Goods Factory Association, agreeing to join in to uphold national rights and redress public grievances. However, due to the short notice, some organizations have not had time to convene meetings to discuss the matter and have requested an extension so that they can participate unanimously after making a decision. The Overseas Chinese Federation has decided to wait several more days and then jointly send a letter to convene a rally to actively boycott the Java Company, hoping to achieve a final victory.

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce received a telegram from the Batavia Chinese General Chamber of Commerce regarding the Xiao Case:

To the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce: In the Zhibade Xiao Case, the shipping company authorities have demoted the chief mate and transferred the case to the Batavia Court for adjudication. The truth will be revealed soon. It is hoped that the matter will be handled with caution. Our association also hopes for a legal and peaceful resolution to avoid significant commercial losses for both parties. Awaiting reply. Batavia Chinese General Chamber of Commerce.

Silver Turns into Platinum

▲Value of Over 54,000 Gold Yuan ▲Russian Con Man's High Skill ▲Also Involved are Lawyer Luo Xi and Others

A Russian con man named Yixia Ning, residing at No. 381 Maierxi Ai Road in the French Concession, makes a living by fraud. Last month, he was carrying a bundle containing several hundred taels of fake platinum, loitering around the Aiduya Road area. He was spotted by Detective Juli Naici (transliteration) of the gambling squad of the French Police. The detective questioned him, but Yixia gave evasive answers. He was immediately taken to the police station. The bundle was opened, and after examination, it was sent to the Public Works Department for chemical analysis. It was discovered that the platinum was fake, made entirely of Chinese silver plated by the defendant. After being questioned by Detective Chief Xi, Yixia confessed that his accomplice made the fake platinum, and he intended to sell it to the Aidinggong Xierte Company in London, England. The platinum weighed 146 taels for No. 21, 144 taels for No. 22, and 143 taels each for Nos. 23 and 24, with a value of 54,625 gold yuan. The British consul had already signed the documents, and the United Import and Export Company on Bowuguan Road was arranging to send it by post or ship. The fake platinum had been insured for over 16,000 taels with an insurance company. If the fraud was discovered in London, they could claim that it had been swapped en route and collect the insurance compensation. They could also borrow a large sum from a bank in Shanghai by mortgaging the platinum. He claimed that the accomplices in the scheme included several people, including a foreign lawyer named Duoxi. The detective chief summoned the lawyer for questioning and then released him pending further instructions. Other accomplices were also ordered to be arrested, but they all fled. Yesterday, the police transferred Xia and Lawyer Du to the French court for investigation. Detective Chief Sacaier first presented the facts of the case, followed by questions from the Chinese and Western officials to the defendants. They were ordered to be detained and held for a future hearing.

Tan Meiying Files for Divorce

▲Zhao Guangzu Remains Unenlightened

Zhao Guangzu, who was previously infatuated with the prostitute Mei Fei, even went so far as to sign a deed of renunciation. He was also swindled out of money by the prostitute and Hu San (Yongquan), who spent it lavishly. He remains unenlightened. His wife, Tan Meiying, found out about it and hired Lawyer Lu Qi to sue the prostitute and others. Hu fled to avoid punishment, and Mei Fei was sentenced to two months in prison, suspended for two years. However, the prostitute is not satisfied with the verdict and is currently appealing. Zhao Guangzu is not grateful to his wife for protecting the family assets. Instead, he resents her and constantly picks quarrels with her, even resorting to violence. Ms. Tan feels that she can no longer live with him and has hired a lawyer to sue Zhao in the Special District Court for divorce. The main reasons are: 1. Zhao has physically assaulted her, causing injuries. 2. Zhao is willfully dissipated and neglects his family. 3. Zhao previously signed a written statement stating that divorce could be granted if there was a legitimate reason. The court will hear the case soon.

Qingyun Lane House Demolition Case to be Pronounced

▲ Many Westerners Testify ▲ Eleven Families Join as Plaintiffs

▲ Yesterday's Debate Concluded ▲ Judgment Set for Next Tuesday

The New Sassoon firm lease broker Xing Dingcheng, who stirred up a sensation in Shanghai, led more than two hundred White Russian desperados, riding in seven or eight freight trucks, at ten o'clock in the morning on September 10th, to Qingyun Lane, Chongming Road, North Sichuan Road, for the illegal demolition of houses, injuring people, and robbery of property. After four hearings by the Shanghai Special District Court, yesterday was the fifth court hearing. The audience of tenants was as crowded as before, and representatives from all walks of life were also present in court to observe. At half past two in the afternoon, Judge Cheng took the bench and began the case. First, he asked the fireman's resume requested by the defendant's lawyer, Ding Rong. He replied that he was Russian and had been the deputy officer of the fire brigade for three years and nine months. His name was Ji Ni Kefu. He was asked, "Did you witness the demolition of houses in Qingyun Lane?" He replied, "I was strolling on that day and happened to pass by that place twice. The first time I saw few people. After I reported to the fire brigade, they immediately sent me with a fire truck. The second time I arrived, I saw many White Russians demolishing houses on the roof, and the order was extremely chaotic." He was asked, "There was no fire, why did you report to the brigade to send a fire truck?" He replied, "I was afraid of a fire, so I borrowed a phone from an electric company at the intersection to report to the brigade. When I arrived at the scene with the truck and saw no fire, I immediately drove back."

At that time, the chaos was even worse. A police patrol car also arrived, led by a Western patrol chief with more than thirty Chinese and Western police officers to suppress the scene. As for whether the defendant Xing Dingcheng was at the scene, he did not pay attention because there were many Chinese, and so on. Then,

the Western Division Chief of the Police Department testified. He was asked, "What is your name and what is your position?" He replied, "My name is Otu, and I am the district chief of the General Police Department." He was asked, "Did you see the demolition of houses in Qingyun Lane?" He replied, "Yes, Qingyun Lane is under the direct jurisdiction of the Hongkou Police Department, but the General Police Department also has jurisdiction. At ten o'clock that morning, I was in the office when someone reported that a fight had occurred on Chongming Road. I immediately led Chinese and Western police officers to the scene to suppress it. After arriving, I learned that

it was White Russians demolishing houses. I ordered the White Russians to stop working. I told them that the houses could not be demolished, and I ordered the White Russians to disperse quickly. I reported to the General Police Department that day, but only in general terms, and the scope was very small. As for the defendant Xing Dingcheng, I did not see him, nor did I pay attention to him," and so on. Then, the clerk of the Kung Ho Foreign Firm testified, giving his name as Qi Ni Kefen, a British citizen, working as a clerk at Kung Ho Foreign Firm. He was asked, "Are you really a clerk or an engineer?" He replied, "Working as a clerk is true." He was asked, "How did you know about the demolition of the houses that day?" He replied, "That day I was in the office, and someone called me and asked me to go. After measuring, I think it was the New Sassoon Foreign Firm that called,

asking me to demolish the houses, but I did not pay attention to whether the defendant Xing Dingcheng joined or not." Then, the plaintiff's witness Yang Quan testified. He was asked, "What is your name, position, and where do you live?" He replied, "My name is Yang Quan, from Jiangsu, and I operate

a Lu Gao Jian meat shop at the mouth of Renzhi Lane on North Sichuan Road, across from Qingyun Lane. I live in the upper floor of the shop." He was asked, "Did you see the demolition of houses in Qingyun Lane?" He replied, "Around ten o'clock on the morning of September 10th, I was reading a newspaper in the shop when suddenly three or four private cars arrived. One stopped at the door of my shop, and the rest stopped across the street, along the mouth of Qingyun Lane. Two Chinese and six or seven Westerners sitting inside jumped out hurriedly and ran into the lane. After a while, a large group of White Russians drove in, carrying long bamboo ladders and rushing into the lane,

then climbing onto the roof to carry out the demolition work. The situation was extremely chaotic. I then learned that a house demolition was taking place. About thirty minutes later, a large team of police officers arrived and the situation calmed down. As for whether the defendant was at the scene, I cannot specify, but I saw two Chinese emerging from the car, one wearing a Western suit and the other wearing Chinese clothes. Judging by their backs, they were slim and small in stature. I did not see their faces clearly, so I cannot identify them as to who they were. What I have said is all the true situation on that day, and I have nothing else to say." The interrogation reached this point.

Eleven shops joined as plaintiffs, including Guangyu Store on North Sichuan Road, Zhang Jiamo, Zhou Sanji, Zhou Ganchen, Shengfa Barber Shop, Zhu Qipeng, Qiantai Xing Store, Yin Zhixian, Tao San Restaurant, Li Shiqiao, Guangtai Rice Store, Ge Peiyuan, Xingfa Store, Tang Huilian, Qifa Store, Gao Jieyuan, Jiangnanchun Western Restaurant, Liangfa Store, and Huiran Hospital, among eleven businesses, participated as plaintiffs, demanding compensation for losses and requesting an injunction against the demolition of houses. Judge Cheng interrogated them one by one, which lasted for two hours before it was completed. Among them, the testimonies of Tang Huilian and Li Shiqiao

were the most indignant and described the attitude of the police on that day. Judge Cheng then announced the start of the debate, conducted by the plaintiffs' lawyers Wang Zuxun and Xue Jiaqi, and the defendants' defense lawyers Ding Rong, Wang Fusang, and Chen Zhongyin. After a round of eloquent arguments on both sides, Judge Cheng announced, "The debate is concluded. Next Tuesday at two o'clock in the afternoon, the verdict will be heard in the Second Criminal Court." The defendant Xing Dingcheng will remain released on bail. As for the protest of lawyer Wang Zuxun that the defendant's agent, lawyer Ding, was suspected of colluding with witnesses in violation of Article 176 of the Criminal Code, the article is not repeated.

Confrontation of Key Criminals in the Kidnapping Case of Qu Chengqing

▲ Convicted Criminals Brought to Court Yesterday ▲ All Said that Bao Lao Er Was the Leader

▲ Bao Claimed It Was a False Accusation Due to Grievances ▲ Result: All Were Detained for Further Interrogation

Qu Chengqing, an employee of Tianxiang Foreign Firm, was kidnapped by bandits on Hai'ning Road on the night of January 11th of this year. He was later rescued by the police, and fourteen kidnappers were successively arrested and sentenced. At that time, several bandits confessed that the case was led by Bao Lao Er, Shi, and A Rong, accomplices of a certain detective. However, Shi fled far away upon hearing the news and has not been found. Bao had already been captured by the police and handed over to the Special District Court for further investigation. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Tingqi opened the court for further hearing. The police specially brought four bandits involved in this case, who were imprisoned in the Western prison, to court for questioning. First, the Zhang-surnamed criminal confessed that Shi A Lao, also known as Bai Tou Mao Rong Sheng, was the assistant of a certain detective and my master. Bao Lao Er was also an accomplice of a certain detective. Before kidnapping Qu, they called me to go with them. They said it was to arrest someone, so at first, I did not know it was a kidnapping. I did not get any money. Now I have been sentenced to death and am waiting for execution in prison, and so on. Two Wang-surnamed bandits also confessed that they were called by Shi and Bao to kidnap Qu, and the ransom note was hidden in Bao's house. They were not allowed to leave. If they disobeyed, they would be threatened with guns. Later, they took advantage of the opportunity to sneak out and were arrested. They have now been sentenced, one to death and one to life imprisonment, etc. Finally, He Qingsi (a former detective, sentenced to life imprisonment for this case) confessed that he had met Bao and Shi once at the Yingbin Hotel, and the topic discussed was purely the purchase of a car. Judge Wu then interrogated the defendant Bao Lao Er, who admitted to working as a detective, but confessed that after Qu Chengqing was kidnapped, I learned about the kidnappers' whereabouts and reported it to the detectives, so the case was solved. The bandits have been harboring resentment ever since, so they falsely accused me of being the leader. If I were indeed at the scene, the kidnapped person would naturally recognize me. Please summon Qu for questioning, and the truth will be clear, and so on. The court ordered the defendant to be taken back into custody, and the criminals remained imprisoned in the Western prison, to be interrogated again at a later date.

Soviet Russian Trade Agency Suddenly Receives a Bomb

▲ Extortion Letter in English but Signed with a Russian Name ▲ Li Wen Claims It's Against the Agency, Not Him Personally

The "Da Mei Evening News" reported that a bomb was found outside the office of the Soviet Russian Trade Agency at No. 2 Beijing Road on Tuesday evening. An attached threatening letter was found. Fearing further acts of violence by the bandits, the agency personnel have requested special protection from the police. The bomb was placed in a wooden box by a teenager dressed in rags who spoke broken English. He first asked the landlord of the property to deliver it to the Soviet Russian Trade Agency, but the landlord refused. The person then went upstairs to deliver it himself. An elevator operator saw him heading in the direction indicated by the landlord. A few minutes later, a coolie discovered the box and handed it over to Li Wen, the Shanghai manager of the Soviet Russian Trade Agency, the next morning. A letter was attached to the box, addressed to Mr. Li Wen for his receipt. It said, "Mr. Li Wen, a second real gift will be presented. Please wait a moment," and was signed with the letters B. R. P. The letter was in English, but the signature was in Russian. Li Wen reported to the police. Today, the police stated that the bomb was not dangerous, but Mr. Li suspects that someone secretly wants to destroy the agency. He personally has no enemies, but the agency, because it is established by the Soviet Russians, must be hated by the White Russians. In addition, a telegram from the Soviet Russian News Agency stated that after receiving this news, the Russian newspapers, especially the Moscow newspapers, are now criticizing the Chinese government for its inadequate protection of Soviet Russian people and institutions.

Youth Drowns in Raging Waves

▲ No Way to Rescue Him

The Taikoo Company's fast Dahao class ferry, yesterday afternoon at three o'clock, carrying passengers from the company's Huatong Wharf in Lan Ni Du, Pudong, was returning to the Xiyangjingbang Wharf when suddenly, near a Japanese warship buoy outside the Xin Kai He, an unnamed youth, taking advantage of people's unpreparedness, suddenly jumped into the raging waves to commit suicide. The captain, Zhao Shengsheng, immediately stopped the ferry and, together with a nearby sampan, tried to rescue him. However, the youth's body was not seen for a long time, so it was impossible to rescue him. It is reported that the deceased was wearing a blue cloth gown, a black mandarin jacket, and a small hat, and was about twenty years old. Because he did not utter a word or leave a suicide note, his name, place of origin, and reason for suicide are completely unknown.

Rickshaw Owner Kidnapped by Bandits for Ransom

▲ Ransom Reduced to Seventy-one Yuan ▲ Still Unable to Pay in Full Despite Scrimping and Saving

▲ Reported to Police Out of Discontent, Two Arrested

Yan Luxiang, a 46-year-old from Funing, resides at No. 76 Caojiadu, West Shanghai, and makes a living by renting out rickshaws. He is married to Madam Chen, and the couple has a close relationship. Unexpectedly, Yan, despite his modest economic circumstances, has also become the target of bandits' greed, and the details of the situation, as well as the small sum of money extorted, are indeed rare among kidnapping cases.

▲ Kidnapped in the Early Morning Yan Luxiang has been in the rickshaw business for sixteen years. He is usually frugal and diligent in his work, getting up at dawn to take care of his renters, which has become his routine. Around four o'clock in the morning on the 3rd of this month, just as he was getting out of bed, three bandits suddenly arrived, one dressed in military uniform, looking like a soldier, one wearing a black robe, and another with a pockmarked face. Claiming to be the adjutant of the army, the one in military uniform and the one with the pockmarked face each pulled out a pistol, aimed it at Yan's chest, and said, "Be sensible and come with me." Yan was panicked and didn't know what to do, so he had no choice but to obey. His wife, Madam Chen, witnessed her husband being robbed but had no way to call for help and feared being harmed, so she could only lament her helplessness.

▲ Torture Repeated After the bandits kidnapped Yan, they first took him to a teahouse in the Sampan Factory New Bridge area, where they sat for a while, and then hid him in room No. 26 of the Changzhou Hotel on North Zhejiang Road, threatening him in every way and repeatedly torturing him. However, Yan valued money as his life, and he was always poor, so no matter how they coerced him, he only listened to fate.

▲ Ransom Reduced Gradually The bandits saw that Yan was unable to redeem himself, and they had been hiding in the hotel for five days, which had cost them a lot of money, and they were also afraid of exposure. Therefore, they reduced the ransom from 300 yuan to 200 yuan and then to 100 yuan, but Yan still could not agree. At this point, although the bandits were filled with anger and considered themselves unlucky, they were still unwilling to let him go easily. So they asked Yan if he had any relatives in Shanghai. Yan replied that his cousins Chen Jiahe and Fu Zhaolian might be able to find a way to help him.

▲ Ransom Payment at the Teahouse At eight o'clock in the morning, a bandit named Yan Chongsan released Yan, led him to a certain teahouse on Touji Bridge, summoned Chen, Fu, Yan's wife Madam Chen, and his younger brother Luxian. After negotiations, the ransom was set at 71 yuan. Chen Jiahe first paid 16 yuan, Yan Bei paid 25 yuan, and finally, Yan's wife collected 7 yuan, totaling 48 yuan. There was still a shortage of 23 yuan, which they could not pay at that time, so they agreed to pay the remaining amount at the Tianbao Teahouse on Yaojia Stone Bridge in Zhabei at three o'clock in the afternoon on the day before yesterday (the 13th). Yan Chongshan put the money into his pocket. Before leaving, he said that if the money was not paid by the deadline, he would take drastic measures and told them his address before leaving.

▲ Reported to the Police for Arrest Although Yan Luxiang suffered a small loss after escaping from captivity, he was very unwilling, so he reported to Squad Leader He Xiong of the Investigation Team of the Fourth District of Zhabei the day before yesterday. He immediately led detectives Li Guiqing, Li Zongnian, Jiao Yunshan, Zhou Guicai, Zhang Bingqing, etc., to No. 44 Xingde Lane, Guangzhao Road, and arrested Yan Ziyu and Yan Hongsheng (also known as Yan Ziru) and brought them to the station.

▲ People in the Military According to Yan Ziyu's confession, he was a batman in the Headquarters of the Newly Compiled Third Brigade of the Anti-Rebel Army and had been serving at the front. He denied kidnapping Yan Luxiang and presented a passport to the case. According to Yan Hongsheng's confession, he was also a soldier of the Newly Compiled Third Brigade, and his confession was evasive. According to Yan Luxiang's confession, he firmly stated that Yan and others were assistants in the kidnapping case, and the principal offender, Gu Chongsan, had escaped. He also presented Gu's card, which read "National Revolutionary Army Anti-Rebel Army Army Newly Compiled Third Brigade Headquarters Major Adjutant". After reviewing the confession, the Director determined that the case involved kidnapping for ransom. In addition to arresting Gu Chongsan, he ordered Yan and others to be sent to the bureau for questioning first.

Tianjin-Pukou Railway Changes Train Schedule

The Tianjin-Pukou Railway Bureau's Traffic Department, in view of the abnormal overcrowding of passengers after the direct train service between Tianjin and Pukou, has decided that from the 17th of this month, the previous Blue Steel cars, which were exclusively for through traffic, will be reused for through passengers. Other vehicles will be changed to regular express and slow trains. All through train times and schedules have also been changed. The No. 202 Up train will depart from Pukou at 7:00 PM every Monday, Wednesday, Friday, and Saturday, and arrive in Tianjin at 7:30 AM on Wednesday, Friday, Sunday, and Monday. The No. 201 Down train will depart from Tianjin at 9:30 PM every Monday, Wednesday, and Friday, and arrive in Pukou at 9:40 AM on Wednesday, Friday, and Sunday.

Reasons for the Public Concession's Ban on Dog Racing

▲ Same Impact as Jai Alai Courts

The Da Mei Wan Bao (North China Daily News) reported that, according to reliable sources, the Shanghai Municipal Council's decision to close the dog racing track was a direct result of someone requesting a license to establish a jai alai court. Within the concession, there are no specific laws against gambling; it relies entirely on the cooperation of the consuls. The Municipal Council usually manages gambling by issuing licenses, so it generally does not issue licenses for gambling places. In the past, some gambling dens relied on certain consuls as protective charms and did not obtain licenses. Now, the Municipal Council naturally cannot grant a license for a jai alai court under any circumstances. However, dog racing tracks and jai alai courts are similar in nature, so it is inconvenient to treat them differently, hence the discussion to ban dog racing.

Liang Shuxian's Embezzlement Case: Court Announcement of Judgment

▲ Liang Should Repay 140,000 Yuan

Liang Shuxian, the head of the Revenue and Expenditure Section of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration, had been in his position for sixteen years since his appointment on the first day of the Republic, and was known as an "unshakeable figure." No matter which director took office, he was never transferred. Unexpectedly, Liang absconded without a trace on April 8th of this year. At the same time, his cashier, Yin Peimin, also abandoned his post and fled. Director Liu Weizhi investigated his accounts and found that he had embezzled 160,000 yuan when he fled this year. Later, because the guarantor only had a guarantee worth 20,000 yuan, there was still a shortage of 140,000 yuan. An arrest warrant was issued, but he has not been caught. Now, Director Liu has hired a lawyer to request a public announcement of the judgment in the Civil Court of the District Court. A judgment has been made that Liang Shuxian should repay 140,000 yuan. As for Yin Peimin, because of his low position and minor role, he is not held responsible. The announcement has now been posted.

Yang Chenqing Has Given Birth to a Son

▲ Accusation of Abandonment Against Lu Shijun ▲ Another Problem in the Future

Yang Chenqing, a former female employee of the Mei Di Bookstore, and her male colleague, Lu Shijun from Wuxi, fell in love and got engaged. However, both parties were impatient and cohabited. When Yang became pregnant, Lu abandoned her. Yang hired a lawyer to file a criminal complaint with the Special District Court. The court has held two hearings, but Lu has failed to appear. Yang's pregnancy has now reached full term, and she went to the Ximen Women and Children's Hospital and gave birth to a son. It is said that after Yang became pregnant, Lu asked Yang that if she gave birth to a son, he should be raised by him. Now that they are involved in litigation, Yang will naturally not agree. Therefore, this piece of flesh will still be subject to disputes in the future.

Shanghai Postal District Offers Small Remittance Drafts

The Shanghai Postal Authority stated that there are 83 towns in the Shanghai postal district. Small remittance drafts have been offered since November 1st of this year in those areas where remittances were not previously available. Detailed procedures can be inquired at the post office.

The New Building in the Russian Incident Is Not the Academia Sinica

Previously, this newspaper reported that a Russian on Route Ghisi (now West Yan'an Road) in Shanghai refused to pay wages and used a gun to injure people, mistakenly stating that the new building there belonged to the Academia Sinica. Yesterday, President Cai of the Academia Sinica sent a telegram from Nanjing to this newspaper to correct the record. The original telegram is as follows: To Shen Bao Newspaper Office: The November 13th report in your local news about a Russian using a gun to injure people involving the Academia Sinica is inconsistent with the facts. The building of our academy on Route Ghisi in Shanghai is a steel testing ground, which has long been completed and contracted by Zhu Senji Construction Company. As for the Russian who caused the incident, it is said that he is a worker at a nearby bakery set up by Westerners and has nothing to do with our academy. Please correct this. Cai Yuanpei.

Rice Industry Wharf Completion Ceremony Today

The Shanghai Rice Industry Association submitted a request to the authorities to allocate the section from Xuejia浜 to Santai Wharf for the construction of a rice industry wharf. Construction has now been completed, and the completion ceremony will be held on the 15th of this month (today), and rice boats will begin to dock. Yesterday, letters were sent to the rice merchants, informing all rice boats. However, the bean and rice businesses are mostly located in the Doushi Street area. With the completion of the rice boat wharf, rice boats will gather in one place after arriving in Shanghai. Therefore, all businesses dealing in rice and grain agreed the other day to move to the area south of the South Guild Hall to Xuejia浜 to facilitate operations. Empty houses in the Xuejia浜 area have been rented out in recent days, and rice shops have been opened. Recently, rice shops in Doushi Street have been moving there one after another, and the market in that area has suddenly become lively.

A Bundle of Telegrams from the Directorate General of Telegraphs

The Shanghai-Fuzhou telegraph line had been disrupted for half a year due to military operations by Lu Xingbang, resulting in a lack of communication. Telegrams to and from Guangzhou were transmitted by submarine cable, costing two jiao (cents) per word, which is twice as expensive as land lines, causing considerable inconvenience to the business community. Recently, the military situation has been resolved, and direct telegraphic communication between Shanghai and Fuzhou was restored yesterday morning. The Directorate General of Telegraphs in Shanghai is now processing telegrams to Fuzhou, Xiamen, Quanzhou, Shantou, Guangdong, and other provinces in Fujian and Guangdong as usual. The direct Shanghai-Qingdao landline was also repaired yesterday morning. Reports can be sent directly without needing to be relayed through Yantai, which is exceptionally fast.

It is said that the Hankou-Chongqing telegraph line has been damaged for several years due to repeated internal turmoil and has recently been repaired in stages. Telegrams to Chongqing, Chengdu, and Sichuan can now arrive on the same day.

Lawyer Ye Fikang Receives Reprimand

▲ The Resolution Has Been Delivered Yesterday

Ye Fikang, a member of the Shanghai Bar Association, was appointed as the defense lawyer for the counter-revolutionary criminal Yan Xiaochu on October 27th of last year. At that time, a contract was established, stipulating that the total public fee for the three-trial conclusion was 5,600 yuan. Later, because Yan Xiaochu was shot, his family members asked Lawyer Ye to return the public fee, but Ye did not allow it. His family members then presented a request to the prosecutor of the Shanghai District Court, asking him to recover the money. The prosecutor believed that the counter-revolutionary case only had two trials, and Lawyer Ye clearly had illegal intentions. Therefore, the prosecutor of the Shanghai District Court requested the Chief Prosecutor of the High Court to submit it to the Jiangsu Lawyers Disciplinary Committee attached to the High Court for disciplinary action. On the 5th of this month, the chairman of the committee, Lin Biao, Fei Wen, Shen Yuan, Li Mian, Zheng Chi, and other members held a meeting and decided that Lawyer Ye Fikang should be reprimanded. The resolution has now been delivered yesterday (the 13th). The following is a copy:

Jiangsu Lawyers Disciplinary Committee Resolution No. 19 Law Character No. 2: Regarding Lawyer Ye Fikang, the lawyer who was subject to disciplinary action due to violating laws and regulations was submitted for disciplinary action by the Chief Prosecutor of the Shanghai District Court. The decision of this committee is as follows: "Main text" Lawyer Ye Fikang shall be subject to a reprimand. "Facts" Lawyer Ye Fikang was appointed on October 18th as the defense lawyer for Yan Xiaochu, who was sued for a revolutionary case, agreeing that 600 yuan would be paid first until the third trial judgment, and after the release, a public fee of 5,000 yuan would be paid, and the public fee contract was attached to the file. Shi Yin Yan Xiaochu was shot on the same day after the contract was signed, and the lawsuit did not proceed. His family members asked for the unpaid public fee of 300 yuan, but it was not allowed. Therefore, the Chief Prosecutor of the Shanghai District Court submitted a request to the Chief Prosecutor of the High Court to submit it for disciplinary action on the grounds that the lawyer received public fees and had fraudulent conduct towards the client. "Reasons" According to the Shanghai Bar Association's Provisional Regulations, Article 31, paragraph 1, item B, item 2, the total amount of public fees charged by lawyers for handling criminal cases must be specified separately according to the trial level. In this case, the disciplined lawyer Ye Fikang and the client entered into a public fee contract, and it was agreed that it would be until the third trial judgment. Regardless of whether the contract stated that the client committed a counter-revolutionary incident, the trial level was only two trials, and there was no third trial, and the amount of public fees agreed upon was a general package, and it was not divided according to the trial area in accordance with the above-mentioned regulations. It is a breach of good faith and violates the provisions of Article 18 of the Lawyers' Regulations. This committee believes that a reprimand should be imposed in accordance with Article 37, paragraph 1 of the same regulations, and a decision is made as follows. November 5, 19th year of the Republic of China, Jiangsu Lawyers Disciplinary Committee Chairman Lin Biao, Fei Wen, Shen Yuan, Li Mian, Zheng Chi.

Russian Woman Commits Suicide Under Train

At around 8 AM yesterday morning, a train from the Wusong Zhanghuabang Railway Factory to Shanghai, while passing near the Tiantong'an Station, suddenly a young Western woman rushed across the road and threw herself onto the tracks to commit suicide. The driver of the train was caught off guard and could not stop in time, so the woman's legs were crushed and her waist was broken, so she was divided into several sections, and the blood and flesh were a mess, which was unbearable to look at. After the accident, the train stopped immediately, and then the body was taken out and placed on the side of the road. It was found that the deceased was about twenty years old, was Russian, and was wearing a cyan gray woolen coat, a white silk shirt, colorful dance stockings, and leather shoes, and her attire was quite fashionable. The local police reported the incident to the Fifth District Police Station. At this time, the deceased's husband had already heard the news and rushed to the scene. It is said that the deceased woman's name was Anre, she was thirty-three years old, and because she had been sick for many years, she did not want to live, so she committed suicide. The deceased's husband's name is Eamerink, and he currently lives on Avenue Joffre in the French Concession, requesting to be exempted from examination and to collect the body himself.

News from Various Labor Unions

▲ Shanghai Postal Workers' Union The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union held its sixth executive committee meeting at its hall at 3:00 PM the day before yesterday. Committee members Qi Jiamou, Zhu Xuefan, Zhang Kechang, Xiao Qingshan, Liu Xinquan, Shui Xiangyun, Zhuang Zhengyin, Xing Rongzhao, Zhao Liancheng, Wang Junchen, Sun Hanliang, and He Jichuan attended.
